# 272\n
{Cambridge, Corpus Christi College 402, fols. 1r-117: Ancrene Wisse}\n
C13b?\n
352 275 N\n
{=S Salop=}\n
{=Sample tagged: fols. 1r-32r=}\n
{=Script - early Textura semi-quadrata=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=The scribe does not like to leave gaps at the end of lines. He does\n
sometimes split words to avoid this, but is much less inclined to do\n
it than most other scribes. Instead he occasionally uses line-fillers\n
such as tiny diagonal strokes, but more often enlarges by some means\n
the final letter of the line. He makes extended cross strokes on final\n
E or T (not noted) he capitalises and extends N, R and F (noted as *N,\n
*R and *F, and he often uses an extended S which lies on its back.\n
It is not like his usual capital S, so I have not recorded it as *S,\n
but as S with a separate note indicating it is a line-filler type of S.\n
The microfilm I have used is very faint and the details noted by\n
Tolkien (1962) are often not visible on the film=}\n
{~f1r~}\n
{>)(*LIBER *OCTAUUS()>}\n
{=ins, in top margin in a later hand=}\n
{>)(*LIBER ECCLesIE *SanCtI *IACOBI DE WYGEMOR . QUEm *IOHannES *PURCEL\n
DEDIT \\ EIDEm ECCLesIE AD INSTANCIAm FRatrIS *WALTerI DE *LODEL~\n
SENIORIS TUnC PreCEnTORIS , \\ *SIQu^IS DiCtuM LIBRUm ALIENAUerIT A\n
PreDiCtA ECClesiA . UeL TITULUm HUnC MALICiOSE \\ DELEUerIT .\' ANATHEMA\n
SIT . *AMen . FIAT . FIAT . FIAT . *AME*N .()}\n
{=ins, in lower margin in a late C13 hand, saying that the book\n
was given to the House of Augustian Canons at Wigmore by John Purcel on\n
the instigation of Brother Walter of Ludlow, senior precentor. The\n
Purcels were of S. Salop. JP late C13 held land at Norbury nr. Bishop\'s\n
Castle and at Diddlebury nr. Ludlow=}\n

$unmae:rehae:lu?/n<pr_HUN+MERE-HEILE $un-?/xp-n_HUN+ $hae:lu/n<pr-k_-HEILE\n
{=Tolkien (1962) reads HIMMERE, but makes no suggestion as to origins\n
or meaning. The minims can be plausibly split as I read it here and it\n
would then be easy to adopt the reading suggested in MED of unmae:re.\n
But there is likely to be some corruption as Cleopatra also has\n
HIMMERE or HUNMERE HEALE while N and T leave it out. Neither the\n
Corpus scribe nor the Cleopatra scribe have HUN- for UN- elsewhere,\n
though excresent H- forms are known in other EME texts and in the SWML\n
especially in Digby 86. It could also possibly be read as UNIUERE for\n
UNFERE meaning "sick", "diseased", "harmful". Millett (2005) emends to\n
HINENE HULEN on the basis of that the scriptural passage analysed here\n
should include the "tabernacula pastorum". This may very well be a satisfactory\n
textual emendation and possibly what was intended by the author. It does\n
not, however, help us to work out what the Corpus scribe thought he was\n
writing here=}\n
{.}\n
$/P13OiF_HIRE\n
